<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">\n         Naval Research Laboratory\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:center;border-bottom:1px solid #aaa;line-height:1.5em;">\n         <a class="image" Research Laboratory logo\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Active\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         1923\xe2\x80\x93present\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Country\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         United States\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Branch\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Navy\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Type\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Research and development\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Size\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         2,538 civilian\n         <br/>\n         86 military (2015)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Part\xc2\xa0of\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         Office of Naval Research\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#B0C4DE;text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;font-size:110%;">\n         Commanders\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Commander\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.nrl.navy.mil/content.php?P=CO" rel="nofollow">\n          Scott D. Moran\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em;">\n         Director of Research\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <a class="external text" href="http://www.nrl.navy.mil/content.php?P=DOR" rel="nofollow">\n          Dr. Bruce Danly\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        United States Naval Research Laboratory\n       </b>\n       (\n       <b>\n        NRL\n       </b>\n       ) is the corporate research laboratory for the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n        United States Navy\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">\n        United States Marine Corps\n       </a>\n       and conducts a wide range of basic scientific research, applied research, technological development and prototyping. A few of the laboratory\'s current specialties include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plasma_physics" title="Plasma physics">\n        plasma physics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_physics" title="Space physics">\n        space physics\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Materials_science" title="Materials science">\n        materials science\n       </a>\n       , and tactical\n       <a href="/wiki/Electronic_warfare" title="Electronic warfare">\n        electronic warfare\n       </a>\n       . NRL is one of the first US Government scientific R&amp;D laboratories, having opened in 1923 at the instigation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n        Thomas Edison\n       </a>\n       , and is currently under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Naval_Research" title="Office of Naval Research">\n        Office of Naval Research\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRL\'s research expenditures are approximately $1.1\xc2\xa0billion per year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Research">\n        Research\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Research">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG/220px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG/330px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG/440px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory_dish_2015.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Part of the Naval Research Laboratory main campus in Washington, DC. The prominent satellite dish is often used as a symbol of the laboratory.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Naval Research Laboratory conducts a wide variety of basic and scientific research and technological development of importance to the Navy. It has a long history of scientific breakthroughs and technological achievements dating back to its foundation in 1923.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-little_book_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-little_book-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In many instances the laboratory\'s contributions to military technology are declassified decades after those technologies have become widely adopted. In 2011, NRL researchers published 1,398 unclassified scientific &amp; technical articles, book chapters and conference proceedings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2008, the NRL was ranked No. 3 among all U.S. institutions holding\n       <a href="/wiki/Nanotechnology" title="Nanotechnology">\n        nanotechnology\n       </a>\n       -related patents, behind\n       <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">\n        IBM\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">\n        University of California\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Current areas of research at NRL include:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Advanced radio, optical and infrared sensors\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Autonomous systems\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Computer science and artificial intelligence\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Directed energy technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Electronic electro-optical device technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Electronic warfare\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Enhanced maintainability, reliability and survivability technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Environmental effects on naval systems\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Imaging research and systems\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Information technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Marine geosciences\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Materials\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Meteorology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Ocean acoustics\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Oceanography\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Space systems and technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Surveillance and sensor technology\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Undersea technology\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Among a wide range of other specific topics and technologies NRL is currently researching: armor for munitions in transport, high-powered lasers, remote explosives detection, spintronics, the dynamics of explosive gas mixtures, electromagnetic\n       <a href="/wiki/Railgun" title="Railgun">\n        Railgun\n       </a>\n       technology, detection of hidden nuclear materials,\n       <a href="/wiki/Graphene" title="Graphene">\n        graphene\n       </a>\n       devices, high-power\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremely_high_frequency" title="Extremely high frequency">\n        extremely high frequency\n       </a>\n       (35\xe2\x80\x93220\xc2\xa0GHz) amplifiers, acoustic lensing, information-rich orbital coastline mapping, arctic weather forecasting, global aerosol analysis &amp; prediction, high-density plasmas,\n       <a href="/wiki/Millisecond_pulsar" title="Millisecond pulsar">\n        Millisecond pulsars\n       </a>\n       , broadband laser data links, virtual mission operation centers, battery technology, photonic crystals, carbon nanotube electronics, electronic sensors, mechanical nano-resonators, solid-state chemical sensors, organic opto-electronics, neural-electronic interfaces and self-assembling nanostructures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The laboratory houses a wide range of R&amp;D facilities. The most recent additions include the NRL Nanoscience Institute\'s 5000sqft Class 100 nanofabrication cleanroom\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl_nsi_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrl_nsi-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and quiet measurement labs and the Laboratory for Autonomous Systems Research (LASR).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_accomplishments">\n        Notable accomplishments\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Notable accomplishments">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG/220px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG/330px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG/440px-Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory_radomes_2015.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         This building on NRL\'s main campus features prominent\n         <a href="/wiki/Radome" title="Radome">\n          radomes\n         </a>\n         on its roof.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Space_sciences">\n        Space sciences\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Space sciences">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Naval Research Laboratory has a long and ongoing history of major contributions to spacecraft development. It placed the second, fifth and seventh American satellites in Earth orbit, including the first solar-powered satellite, the first surveillance satellite, the first meteorological satellite and the first GPS satellite.\n       <a href="/wiki/Project_Vanguard" title="Project Vanguard">\n        Project Vanguard\n       </a>\n       , the first American satellite program, tasked NRL with the design, construction and launch of an artificial satellite, which was accomplished in 1958. As of 2013,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanguard_I" title="Vanguard I">\n        Vanguard I\n       </a>\n       is still in orbit, making it the longest-lived man-made satellite.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vanguard_II" title="Vanguard II">\n        Vanguard II\n       </a>\n       was the first satellite to observe the Earth\'s cloud cover and therefore the first meteorological satellite. NRL\'s recently declassified\n       <a href="/wiki/Galactic_Radiation_and_Background" title="Galactic Radiation and Background">\n        Galactic Radiation and Background\n       </a>\n       I (GRAB I) was the first U.S.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_satellite" title="Intelligence satellite">\n        intelligence satellite\n       </a>\n       , mapping out Soviet radar networks from space. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">\n        Global Positioning System\n       </a>\n       (GPS) was invented at NRL and tested by NRL\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Timation" title="Timation">\n        Timation\n       </a>\n       series of satellites. The first operational GPS satellite, Timation IV (NTS-II) was designed and constructed at NRL.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL pioneered the study of the sun Ultraviolet and X-Ray spectrum and continues to contribute to the field with satellites like\n       <a href="/wiki/Coriolis_(satellite)" title="Coriolis (satellite)">\n        Coriolis (satellite)\n       </a>\n       launched in 2003. NRL is also responsible for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tactical_Satellite_Program" title="Tactical Satellite Program">\n        Tactical Satellite Program\n       </a>\n       with spacecraft launched in 2006, 2009 and 2011.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Along with Project Vanguard, NRL also designed the first satellite tracking system,\n       <a href="/wiki/Minitrack" title="Minitrack">\n        Minitrack\n       </a>\n       , which became the prototype for future satellite tracking networks. Prior to the success of surveillance satellites, the iconic parabolic antenna atop NRL\'s main headquarters in Washington, D.C. was part of\n       <a href="/wiki/Communication_Moon_Relay" title="Communication Moon Relay">\n        Communication Moon Relay\n       </a>\n       , a project that succeeded in sending and receiving signals bounced off the Moon both for long-distance communications research and surveillance of internal soviet transmissions during the Cold War.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorology">\n        Meteorology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Meteorology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:170825-N-N0101-502_(36086497114).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1024" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg/220px-170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg/330px-170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg/440px-170825-N-N0101-502_%2836086497114%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:170825-N-N0101-502_(36086497114).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NRL satellite image of hurricane Harvey just prior to landfall on the Texas coast, 2017.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Marine Meteorology Division, which is located in Monterey, California, makes important contributions to weather forecasting in the United States and around the world by making publicly available imagery from 18 weather satellites. Satellite images of hurricanes and cyclones that provide advanced warning of impending severe weather often originate the from Naval Research Lab Monterey, as seen recently during hurricane Harvey.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRL is also involved in weather forecasting models such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Weather_Research_and_Forecasting_model" title="Hurricane Weather Research and Forecasting model">\n        Hurricane Weather Research and Forecasting model\n       </a>\n       released in 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL\'s spacecraft development program continues today with the\n       <a href="/wiki/TacSat-4" title="TacSat-4">\n        TacSat-4\n       </a>\n       experimental tactical reconnaissance &amp; communication satellite. In addition to spacecraft design, NRL also designs and operates research instruments, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Large_Angle_and_Spectrometric_Coronagraph" title="Large Angle and Spectrometric Coronagraph">\n        Large Angle and Spectrometric Coronagraph\n       </a>\n       Experiment (LASCO)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       aboard the\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_and_Heliospheric_Observatory" title="Solar and Heliospheric Observatory">\n        Solar and Heliospheric Observatory\n       </a>\n       (SOHO). NASA\'s Gamma-ray Large Area Space Telescope (GLAST) was tested at NRL spacecraft testing facilities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRL scientists have most recently contributed leading research to the study of novas\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and gamma ray bursts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Materials_science">\n        Materials science\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Materials science">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NRL has a long history of contributions to materials science, dating back to the use of\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_radiography" title="Industrial radiography">\n        Industrial radiography\n       </a>\n       with gamma rays for the nondestructive inspection of metal casings and welds on Navy vessels beginning in the 1920s. Modern mechanical\n       <a href="/wiki/Fracture_mechanics" title="Fracture mechanics">\n        fracture mechanics\n       </a>\n       were pioneered at NRL and were subsequently applied to solve fracture problems in Navy vessels, commercial aircraft and Polaris missiles. That knowledge is in widespread use today in applications ranging from design of nuclear reactors to aircraft, submarines and toxic material storage tanks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-little_book_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-little_book-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRL developed the synthesis of high-purity GaAs crystals used in a myriad of modern high frequency transceivers including cellular phones, satellite communication systems, commercial and military radar systems including those aboard all US combat aircraft and ARM, Phoenix, AIM-9L and AMRAAM missiles. NRL\'s GaAs inventions were licensed by Rockwell, Westinghouse, Texas Instruments and Hughes Research.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl.navy.mil_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrl.navy.mil-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       High-purity GaAs is also used for high-efficiency solar cells like those aboard NASA\'s Spirit and Opportunity rovers currently on Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Fundamental aspects of stealth technology were developed at NRL, including the radar absorption mechanisms in ferrite-containing materials.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl.navy.mil_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrl.navy.mil-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Metal bearing surface treatments using Cr ion implantation researched at NRL nearly tripled the service life of Navy turbine engine parts and was adopted for Army helicopter parts as well.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl.navy.mil_18-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrl.navy.mil-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Fluorinated polyurethane coatings developed at NRL are used to line fuel storage tanks throughout the US Navy, reducing leakage and environmental and fuel contamination. The same polymer films are used in Los Angeles-class submarine radomes to repel water and enable radar operation soon after surfacing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrl.navy.mil_18-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nrl.navy.mil-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Scientists at NRL frequently contribute theoretical and experimental research on novel materials,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       particularly\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magnetic_material" title="Magnetic material">\n        magnetic materials\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanomaterial" title="Nanomaterial">\n        nanomaterials\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermoplastic" title="Thermoplastic">\n        thermoplastic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radar">\n        Radar\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Radar">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The first modern U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">\n        radar\n       </a>\n       was invented and developed at NRL in Washington, DC in 1922. By 1939, NRL installed the first operational radar aboard the USS New York, in time for radar to contribute to naval victories of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Coral_Sea" title="Battle of the Coral Sea">\n        Coral Sea\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Midway" title="Battle of Midway">\n        Midway\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Guadalcanal_Campaign" title="Guadalcanal Campaign">\n        Guadalcanal\n       </a>\n       . NRL then further developed over-the-horizon radar as well as radar data displays.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-little_book_3-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-little_book-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NRL\'s Radar Division\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       continues important research &amp; development contributing to US Navy and US Department of Defense capabilities.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tactical_electronic_warfare">\n        Tactical electronic warfare\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tactical electronic warfare">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       NRL\'s Tactical Electronic Warfare (TEW) Division\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is responsible for research and development in support of the Navy\'s tactical electronic warfare requirements and missions. These include electronic warfare support measures, electronic countermeasures, and supporting counter-countermeasures, as well as studies, analyses, and simulations for determining and improving the performance of Electronic Warfare systems. NRL TEW includes aerial, surface, and ground EW within its scope. NRL is responsible for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Identification,_friend_or_foe" title="Identification, friend or foe">\n        identification, friend or foe\n       </a>\n       (IFF) system and a number of other advances.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Information_security">\n        Information security\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Information security">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Information Technology Division\n       </i>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       has a world-class information security R&amp;D group, which is where the IETF\'s IP Security (IPsec) protocols were originally developed. The Encapsulating Security Payload (ESP) protocol developed at NRL is widely used for virtual private network (VPN) connections worldwide.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The projects developed by the laboratory often become mainstream applications without public awareness of the developer; an example in computer science is\n       <a href="/wiki/Onion_routing" title="Onion routing">\n        onion routing\n       </a>\n       , the core principle of the anonymizing Tor software.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nuclear_research">\n        Nuclear research\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Nuclear research">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Nuclear power research was initiated at NRL as early as 1939,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-little_book_3-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-little_book-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       six years before the first atomic bomb, for the purpose of powering submarines. Uranium enrichment methods sponsored by NRL over the course of World War II were adopted by the Manhattan Project\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and guided the design of\n       <a href="/wiki/Oak_Ridge_National_Laboratory" title="Oak Ridge National Laboratory">\n        Oak Ridge National Laboratory\n       </a>\n       \'s Uranium enrichment plant. NRL is currently developing laser focusing techniques aimed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Inertial_confinement_fusion" title="Inertial confinement fusion">\n        inertial confinement fusion\n       </a>\n       technology.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_sciences">\n        Physical sciences\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Physical sciences">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Static_discharger" title="Static discharger">\n        Static discharger\n       </a>\n       seen on trailing edges of virtually all modern aircraft was originally developed by NRL scientists during World War II. After the war, the laboratory developed modern synthetic lubricants\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       initially for use in the Navy\'s jet aircraft but they were subsequently adopted by the commercial jet industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-little_book_3-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-little_book-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the late 1960s, NRL researched low-temperature physics, achieving for the first time a temperature within one millionth of a degree of absolute zero in 1967. In 1985 two scientists at the laboratory,\n       <a href="/wiki/Herbert_A._Hauptman" title="Herbert A. Hauptman">\n        Herbert A. Hauptman\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jerome_Karle" title="Jerome Karle">\n        Jerome Karle\n       </a>\n       , won the Nobel Prize for devising direct methods employing\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-ray_diffraction" title="X-ray diffraction">\n        X-ray diffraction\n       </a>\n       analysis in the determination of crystal structures.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Their methods form the basis for the computer packages used in pharmaceutical labs and research institutions worldwide for the analysis of more than 10,000 new substances each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL has most recently published research on quantum computing,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       quantum dots,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       plasma shockwaves,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       thermodynamics of liquids,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       modeling of oil spills\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and other topics.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL operates a small squadron of research aircraft termed Scientific Development Squadron One\n       <a href="/wiki/VXS-1" title="VXS-1">\n        VXS-1\n       </a>\n       . Its missions include, for example, Rampant Lion, which used sophisticated airborne instrumentation (gravimeters, magnetometers and hyperspectral cameras) to collect precise 3D topography of two-thirds of Aghanistan and locate natural resources (underground gas and mineral deposits, vegetation types, etc) there\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in Iraq and Colombia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Plasma_science">\n        Plasma science\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Plasma science">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Division of Plasma Science conducts research and development into ionized matter. NRL currently holds the world record for most energetic rail gun projectile (33 MJ)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and fastest manmade projectile (334 million MPH).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">\n        Organization\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Organization">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="589" data-file-width="600" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naval_Research_Laboratory.png/220px-Naval_Research_Laboratory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naval_Research_Laboratory.png/330px-Naval_Research_Laboratory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Naval_Research_Laboratory.png/440px-Naval_Research_Laboratory.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_Research_Laboratory.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Naval Research Laboratory seal used before 2016\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The laboratory is divided into four research directorates, one financial directorate, and one executive directorate. All the directorates are headquartered in Washington, D.C. Many directorates have other facilities elsewhere, primarily at either the\n       <i>\n        Stennis Space Center\n       </i>\n       in Bay St Louis, Mississippi or in Monterey, California.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Staff">\n        Staff\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Staff">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Most NRL staff are civilians in the Civil Service, with a relatively small number of Navy enlisted personnel or officers. In addition, there are some support contractors that work on-site at NRL. As of 31 December 2015, across all NRL locations, NRL had 2540 civilian employees (i.e., not including civilian contractors).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the same date, there were 35 military officers on-board NRL and 58 enlisted on-board NRL, most of whom are with NRL\'s VXS-1 Scientific Flight Detachment, which is located aboard the Patuxent River (\'Pax River\') Naval Air Station (NAS) in southern Maryland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL has special authority to use a Pay-Band pay system instead of using the traditional\n       <i>\n        General Schedule (GS)\n       </i>\n       pay system for its civilian employees.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-federalregister.gov_57-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-federalregister.gov-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This gives NRL more ability to pay employees based on performance and merit, rather than time-in-grade or some other seniority metric. There are several different pay-band groups at NRL, each being for different categories of civilian employees. As of 31 December 2015, NRL had 1615 civilian scientists/engineers in the\n       <i>\n        NP\n       </i>\n       pay system, 103 civilian technicians in the\n       <i>\n        NR\n       </i>\n       pay system, 383 civilian administrative specialists/professionals in the\n       <i>\n        NO\n       </i>\n       pay system, and 238 civilian administrative support staff in the\n       <i>\n        NC\n       </i>\n       pay system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NRL scientists &amp; engineers typically are in the\n       <i>\n        (NP)\n       </i>\n       pay group in NRL\'s Pay Band system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-federalregister.gov_57-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-federalregister.gov-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The NP-II pay band is equivalent to GS-5 Step 1 through GS-10 Step 10. The NP-III pay band is equivalent to GS-11 Step 1 through GS-13 Step 10. NRL\'s\n       <i>\n        Pay Band IV\n       </i>\n       corresponds to the GS-14 Step 1 to GS-15 Step 10 pay grades, inclusive, while NRL\'s Pay Band V can pay above GS-15 Step 10 and corresponds to the\n       <i>\n        Senior Technologist (ST)\n       </i>\n       pay grade elsewhere in the US Government\'s Civil Service. A new graduate scientist or engineer with a Bachelor of Science degree typically is hired with a salary equivalent to a GS-7, while a new graduate scientist or engineer with a Master of Science degree typically at the equivalent of a GS-11.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the NRL Fact Book (2016), NRL had 870 employees with a Doctorate, 417 employees with a master\'s degree as their highest degree, and 576 employees with a bachelor\'s degree as their highest degree.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016_56-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NRL_Fact_Book.2C_2016-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The laboratory also hosts post-doctoral researchers and was voted #15 in the Best Places to Work PostDocs 2013 survey.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Research_directorates">\n        Research directorates\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Research directorates">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The four research directorates within NRL are:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Systems Directorate\n        </b>\n        (Code 5000) is responsible for performing a range of activities from basic research through engineering development to expand the operational capabilities of the US Navy. There are four research divisions: Radar, Information Technology, Optical Sciences, and Tactical Electronic Warfare.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Materials Science and Component Technology Directorate\n        </b>\n        (Code 6000) carries out a range of materials research with the aim of better understanding of the materials in order to develop improved and advanced materials for use by the US Navy. There are seven research divisions: Laboratory for the Structure of Matter, Chemistry, Material Science &amp; Technology, Laboratory for Computational Physics and Fluid Dynamics, Plasma Physics, Electronics Science &amp; Technology, and the Center for Biomolecular Science &amp; Engineering.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Ocean and Atmospheric Science and Technology Directorate\n        </b>\n        (Code 7000) performs research in the fields of acoustics, remote sensing, oceanography, marine geosciences, marine meteorology, and space science.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n         <a href="#cite_note-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        There are six research divisions: Acoustics, Remote Sensing, Oceanography, Marine Geosciences, Marine Meteorology, and Space Science.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The mission of the\n        <b>\n         Naval Center for Space Technology\n        </b>\n        (NCST) (Code 8000) is to preserve and enhance a strong space technology base and provide expert assistance in the development and acquisition of space systems for naval missions. There are two research divisions: Space Systems Development and Spacecraft Engineering.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Support_directorates">\n        Support directorates\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Support directorates">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The two support directorates are:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Executive Directorate\n        </b>\n        operations are directed by the Commander of the NRL, who typically is a US Navy Captain. In addition to management functions, the Directorate also manages the Nanoscience Institute (NSI), founded in April 2001 as a multidisciplinary nanotechnology research institute at the intersections of the fields of materials, electronics and biology. Scientific Development Squadron ONE (\n        <a href="/wiki/VXS-1" title="VXS-1">\n         VXS-1\n        </a>\n        ),\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n         <a href="#cite_note-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        located at\n        <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Patuxent_River" title="Naval Air Station Patuxent River">\n         Naval Air Station Patuxent River\n        </a>\n        , Maryland, which provides airborne research facilities to NRL as well as other agencies of the US Government, is also run out of the Executive Directorate.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Business Operations Directorate\n        </b>\n        provides program management for the business programs which support the scientific directorates of NRL. It provides contracting, financial management and supply expertise to the scientific projects.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Locations">\n        Locations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Locations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NavalResearchLab.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2159" data-file-width="3020" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/NavalResearchLab.jpg/220px-NavalResearchLab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/NavalResearchLab.jpg/330px-NavalResearchLab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/NavalResearchLab.jpg/440px-NavalResearchLab.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NavalResearchLab.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Part of the NRL complex seen from the air above the\n         <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n          Potomac River\n         </a>\n         in 2012. The part of the campus shown contains the oldest five buildings on the campus.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NRLP3_landing.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="562" data-file-width="1274" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NRLP3_landing.JPG/220px-NRLP3_landing.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NRLP3_landing.JPG/330px-NRLP3_landing.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/NRLP3_landing.JPG/440px-NRLP3_landing.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NRLP3_landing.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NRL Scientific Development Squadron ONE\n         <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_P-3_Orion" title="Lockheed P-3 Orion">\n          NP-3D Orion\n         </a>\n         of\n         <a href="/wiki/VXS-1" title="VXS-1">\n          VXS-1\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The main campus of NRL is in Washington, DC, near the southernmost part of the District. It is on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac River\n       </a>\n       and is immediately south of (but is not part of)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joint_Base_Anacostia-Bolling" title="Joint Base Anacostia-Bolling">\n        Joint Base Anacostia-Bolling\n       </a>\n       . This campus is immediately north of the Blue Plains site of the DC Water Authority. Exit 1 of northbound I-295 leads directly to Overlook Avenue and the NRL Main Gate.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, NRL operates several field sites and satellite facilities:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        NRL-Stennis is located at NASA\'s\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stennis_Space_Center" title="Stennis Space Center">\n         Stennis Space Center\n        </a>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Bay_St._Louis,_Mississippi" title="Bay St. Louis, Mississippi">\n         Bay St. Louis, Mississippi\n        </a>\n        , and specializes in oceanography, marine geology, geophysics, geoacoustics, and geotechnology.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        NRL-Monterey is located east of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Naval_Postgraduate_School" title="Naval Postgraduate School">\n         Naval Postgraduate School\n        </a>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Monterey,_California" title="Monterey, California">\n         Monterey, California\n        </a>\n        , sharing a campus with the\n        <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Numerical_Meteorology_and_Oceanography_Center" title="Fleet Numerical Meteorology and Oceanography Center">\n         Fleet Numerical Meteorology and Oceanography Center\n        </a>\n        and the San Francisco Bay Area/Monterey local forecast office of the\n        <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">\n         National Weather Service\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n         <a href="#cite_note-63">\n          [63]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        NRL-Monterey is dedicated to meteorology and atmospheric research.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/VXS-1" title="VXS-1">\n         Scientific Development Squadron ONE (VXS-1)\n        </a>\n        is a tenant aboard\n        <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Patuxent_River" title="Naval Air Station Patuxent River">\n         Naval Air Station Patuxent River\n        </a>\n        in Maryland, and operates a wide range of research aircraft.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <i>\n         Chesapeake Bay Detachment (CBD)\n        </i>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Beach,_Maryland" title="Chesapeake Beach, Maryland">\n         Chesapeake Beach, Maryland\n        </a>\n        is 168-acre site for research in radar, electronic warfare, optical devices, materials, communications, and fire research. This facility is often used in combination with the Multiple Research Site on\n        <a href="/wiki/Tilghman_Island,_Maryland" title="Tilghman Island, Maryland">\n         Tilghman Island, Maryland\n        </a>\n        just across the Chesapeake Bay.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <i>\n         Midway Research Center\n        </i>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Quantico,_Virginia" title="Quantico, Virginia">\n         Quantico, Virginia\n        </a>\n        , Free Space Antenna Range in\n        <a href="/wiki/Pomonkey,_Maryland" title="Pomonkey, Maryland">\n         Pomonkey, Maryland\n        </a>\n        , and Blossom Point Satellite Tracking and Command Station in\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Blossom_Point,_Maryland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Blossom Point, Maryland (page does not exist)">\n         Blossom Point, Maryland\n        </a>\n        are used by NRL\'s\n        <i>\n         Naval Center for Space Technology\n        </i>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n         <a href="#cite_note-64">\n          [64]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The Marine Corrosion Facility located on\n        <a href="/wiki/Fleming_Key" title="Fleming Key">\n         Fleming Key\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Station_Key_West" title="Naval Air Station Key West">\n         Naval Air Station Key West\n        </a>\n        in Florida is used by the Center for Corrosion Science &amp; Engineering.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The ex-\n        <a href="/wiki/USS_Shadwell_(LSD-15)" title="USS Shadwell (LSD-15)">\n         USS Shadwell\n        </a>\n        in\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_Bay,_Alabama" title="Mobile Bay, Alabama">\n         Mobile Bay, Alabama\n        </a>\n        is used by the Center for Safety and Survivability to develop and test techniques and equipment for shipboard fire fighting.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        NRL operates several synchrotron radiation\n        <a href="/wiki/Beamline" title="Beamline">\n         beamlines\n        </a>\n        and the Extreme-Ultraviolet and X-Ray Calibration Facility at the\n        <a href="/wiki/National_Synchrotron_Light_Source" title="National Synchrotron Light Source">\n         National Synchrotron Light Source\n        </a>\n        at the\n        <a href="/wiki/Brookhaven_National_Laboratory" title="Brookhaven National Laboratory">\n         Brookhaven National Laboratory\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">\n        Early history\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Early history">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Artifacts found on the NRL campus, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">\n        stone tools\n       </a>\n       and ceramic shards, show that the site had been inhabited since the Late\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archaic_period_in_North_America" title="Archaic period in North America">\n        Archaic Period\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Calvert,_2nd_Baron_Baltimore" title="Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore">\n        Cecil Calvert, 2nd Baron Baltimore\n       </a>\n       granted the tract of land including the present NRL campus to William Middleton in 1663. It became part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/District_of_Columbia" title="District of Columbia">\n        District of Columbia\n       </a>\n       in 1791, and was purchased by Thomas Grafton Addison in 1795, who named the area\n       <a href="/wiki/Bellevue_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Bellevue (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Bellevue\n       </a>\n       and built a mansion on the highlands to the east. Zachariah Berry purchased the land in 1827, who rented it out for various purposes including a\n       <a href="/wiki/Fishery" title="Fishery">\n        fishery\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Plains_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Blue Plains (Washington, D.C.)">\n        Blue Plains\n       </a>\n       . The mansion was demolished during the Civil War to build\n       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Greble" title="Fort Greble">\n        Fort Greble\n       </a>\n       . In 1873 the land was purchased by the federal government as the Bellevue Annex to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_Gun_Factory" title="Naval Gun Factory">\n        Naval Gun Factory\n       </a>\n       , and several buildings were constructed including the Commandant\'s house, "Quarters A", which is still in use today.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation">\n        Foundation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Foundation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="651" data-file-width="994" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png/220px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png/330px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png/440px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1923.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NRL in 1923, the first year of its existence, showing the first five buildings on its campus\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Naval Research Laboratory\n       </i>\n       came into existence from an idea that originated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">\n        Thomas Edison\n       </a>\n       . In a May 1915 editorial piece in the\n       <i>\n        New York Times Magazine\n       </i>\n       , Edison wrote; "The Government should maintain a great research laboratory... In this could be developed...all the technique of military and\n       <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">\n        naval\n       </a>\n       progression without any vast expense."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n        <a href="#cite_note-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This statement addressed concerns about World War I in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Edison then agreed to serve as the head of the Naval Consulting Board that consisted of civilians who had achieved expertise. The focus of the Naval Consulting Board was as advisor to the U.S. Navy pertaining to science and technology. The board brought forward a plan to create a modern facility for the Navy. In 1916 Congress allocated $1.5\xc2\xa0million for implementation. However, construction was delayed until 1920 because of the war and internal disagreements within the board.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. Naval Research Laboratory, the first modern research institution created within the United States Navy, began operations at 1100 on 2 July 1923. The Laboratory\'s two original divisions \xe2\x80\x93 Radio and Sound \xe2\x80\x93 performed research in the fields of high-frequency radio and underwater sound propagation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They produced communications equipment, direction-finding devices, sonar sets, and perhaps most significant of all, the first practical\n       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">\n        radar\n       </a>\n       equipment built in the United States. They performed basic research, participating, for example, in the discovery and early exploration of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ionosphere" title="Ionosphere">\n        ionosphere\n       </a>\n       . Moreover, the NRL was able to work gradually toward its goal of becoming a broadly based research facility. By the beginning of\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       , five new divisions had been added: Physical Optics, Chemistry, Metallurgy, Mechanics and Electricity, and Internal Communications.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_years_and_growth">\n        World War II years and growth\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: World War II years and growth">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="879" data-file-width="1160" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png/220px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png/330px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png/440px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_1944.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NRL in 1944, after significant wartime growth\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Total employment at the NRL jumped from 396 in 1941 to 4400 in 1946, expenditures from $1.7\xc2\xa0million to $13.7\xc2\xa0million, the number of buildings from 23 to 67, and the number of projects from 200 to about 900. During World War II, scientific activities necessarily were concentrated almost entirely on applied research. New electronics equipment \xe2\x80\x93 radio,\n       <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">\n        radar\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sonar" title="Sonar">\n        sonar\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x93 was developed. Countermeasures were devised. New lubricants were produced, as were antifouling paints, luminous identification tapes, and a sea marker to help save survivors of disasters at sea. A thermal diffusion process was conceived and used to supply some of the U-235 isotope needed for one of the first atomic bombs. Also, many new devices that developed from booming wartime industry were type tested and then certified as reliable for the Fleet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="After_WWII">\n        After WWII\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: After WWII">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="1400" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg/220px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg/330px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg/440px-US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Naval_Research_Laboratory_in_2001.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NRL in 2001\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As a result of the scientific accomplishments of the WWII, the United States emerged into the postwar era determined to consolidate its wartime gains in science and technology and to preserve the working relationship between its armed forces and the scientific community. While the Navy was establishing the\n       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Naval_Research" title="Office of Naval Research">\n        Office of Naval Research\n       </a>\n       (ONR) as a liaison with and supporter of basic and applied scientific research, the Navy encouraged NRL to broaden its scope since it was the Navy Department\'s corporate research laboratory. NRL was placed under the administrative oversight of ONR after ONR was created. NRL\'s Commanding Officer reports to the Navy\'s\n       <i>\n        Chief of Naval Research (CNR)\n       </i>\n       . The Chief of Naval Research leads the Office of Naval Research, which primarily is located in the Ballston area of Arlington, Virginia. The reorganization also caused a parallel shift of the Laboratory\'s emphasis to one of long-range basic and applied research in the full range of the physical sciences.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, rapid expansion during the war had left NRL improperly structured to address long-term Navy requirements. One major task \xe2\x80\x93 neither easily nor rapidly accomplished \xe2\x80\x93 was that of reshaping and coordinating research. This was achieved by transforming a group of largely autonomous scientific divisions into a unified institution with a clear mission and a fully coordinated research program. The first attempt at reorganization vested power in an executive committee composed of all the division superintendents. This committee was impracticably large, so in 1949, a civilian director of research was named and given full authority over the program. Positions for associate directors were added in 1954.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-factbook_2-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-factbook-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">\n        Modern era\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Modern era">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 1992, the previously separate\n       <i>\n        Naval Oceanographic and Atmospheric Research Laboratory (NOARL)\n       </i>\n       , with centers in Bay St. Louis, Mississippi, and Monterey, California, was merged into NRL. Since then, NRL is also the lead Navy center for research in Oceanographic and Atmospheric Sciences, with special strengths in physical oceanography, marine geosciences, ocean acoustics, marine meteorology, and remote oceanic and atmospheric sensing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-modern_67-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-modern-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n       <ul of auxiliaries of the United States Navy\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span
